Page 17

Spring and Autumn

Dextral Winding Wind-Fixing Snail 249

— Zhan Lu

Among the clear and rich antiques, there is a dextral winding wind-fixing snail; pearls do not have dextral or sinistral winding distinctions, it is probably a dextral winding wind-fixing snail.

"A small divine snail, four inches, like a fist, divine incense offered to guide the star ship; peace and fulfillment, wind gone, not allowing whale waves to crash across the sky," this is from Chen Zhongbo of Qiantang's "Traces of Ryukyu Shoes"; Zhongbo accompanied the esteemed Qian Xing as an envoy to Ryukyu during the Qing Daoguang era to enshrine the King of Zhongshan. As per usual, a dextral winding white snail was offered in the ship, said to avoid wind and waves. Zhongbo's poem has a self-note: "During the Qianlong era, the Panchen Erdeni presented a dextral winding white snail; shaped like a fist, with a diameter of four inches and two fen, named wind-fixing snail; when Grand General Fukang'an conquered Taiwan, Emperor Gaozong ordered it to be moved from the palace. After the affair, it was left in the Fujian Governor's Office. The box had the words 'Protecting Safe Passage Across Rivers and Seas,' etc." Later, it was moved from the Governor's Office to the Provincial Governor's Office, this was the event in the fifth year of Jiaqing. At the time, Yue Wenkai and Ji Dingyuan were the appointed official and vice envoy to Ryukyu to enshrine the king. A dextral winding white snail was offered in the ship. On the seventh day of the fifth month, they set sail from Fujian. The wind and waves were calm and they arrived in Ryukyu in six days. The journey back was the same. In the eleventh year of Jiaqing, General Mian Chong'a conquered the pirate Cai Qian, Emperor Jiaqing once issued an edict: "Previously, when Fukang'an pacified Lin Shuangwen, he carried a propitious, auspicious, dextral winding snail across the sea. The sails were peaceful and smooth; now, it is distributed and handed to Mian Chong'a to respectfully carry along, to seek blessings for a safe crossing. On the day of the triumphant return after the affair, order a senior official to respectfully send it to the capital," and so on. In the tenth year, Qi Kun and Fei Xizhang were appointed official and vice star envoys to enshrine Ryukyu. A divine snail was offered in the ship. They encountered storms twice but were able to turn danger into safety. In the third collection of Emperor Qianlong's imperial poems and essays, there is a "Praise for the Dextral Winding White Snail," with a self-note: "Each year, the lamas in Tibet present Dan books during the New Year and the Emperor's birthday. Among the offered items, there is a dextral winding white snail. Those crossing the sea carry it on the ship, which brings auspiciousness and stability. It is of utmost importance."

The ability of the dextral winding white snail to fix the wind must be a kind of myth; however, during the Qianlong, Jiaqing, and Daoguang eras of the former Qing dynasty, it was regarded as a rare commodity. It was suddenly left in the outer provinces, and then suddenly handed over to the inner court. The common people did not know, and thought it was a wind-fixing pearl. Now the dextral winding wind-fixing pearl in the Qing Palace antiques is probably the propitious, auspicious, dextral winding white snail presented by the Erdeni of Tibet. At the time, enshrining Ryukyu and conquering Taiwan, the wind-fixing pearl was in the limelight. What about Ryukyu now? Gone! What about Taiwan? Gone! All that remains is this wind-fixing pearl passed down through generations; it is not "great benefit and auspiciousness," but rather "great loss and bad luck!" Wind-fixing pearl, wind-fixing pearl, what is its use? If there really is a wind-fixing pearl, then there must also be a water-avoiding pearl; now, during the "water disaster" in the Yangtze River basin, where can one find a life-saving water-avoiding pearl from Wang Pusa? Alas!

Note 1: Chen Zhongbo's "Hanhuitang Poems". Note 2: Chen Zhi's "Biluoyinguansui Pen". Note 3: Liang Zhangju's "Langjiji Tan".

Summer Has Arrived 250

— Pei Yu

We hear the cuckoo calling "family after family cuckoo", knowing that the plum rain season has arrived, and the farmers are busy with work. When the girls of Denmark hear the first call of the cuckoo, they know that summer has arrived. They must listen carefully and ask the cuckoo to tell them how many more years they have to wait before they can get married; so the Danes say that the cuckoo is so busy answering so many questions that it has no time to build its own nest.

From a legendary point of view, the Danes are much more humorous than the English. Because in the first half of the year, when the lanes and alleys are filled with mud, the English often say: "Wait, wait until the cuckoo finishes cleaning up all the mud before we talk about it." Everyone knows that the cuckoo does not build nests. It is the swallow that cleverly builds nests with mud. Then, when the children hear this, they must wonder why the cuckoo has to go everywhere to clean up the mud? If the Danish explanation had not come first, this mystery would have been difficult to solve.

In Sussex, April 14 is called "Cuckoo Day" and April 15 is called "Swallow Day". There is a story to tell about why it is called "Cuckoo Day": it turns out that an old woman once flew to France on a broom handle and brought the first cuckoo back in a basket, brought it to Heathfield, and released the cuckoo. This day was April 14; and the place where the cuckoo was released is also famous, namely, where Jack Cade was killed in the rebellion. This is the origin of "Cuckoo Day".

The cuckoo is like this in foreign countries, but not so in China. We also call it the "Zi Gui" or "heartbreak bird," and the sound of its call seems to say, "It is better to return." Therefore, the legends about the cuckoo in our country are negative, decadent, and sad; only the legends about the cuckoo bird are positive, exciting, and happy. Now, we still abandon the cuckoo and take the cuckoo bird.

This year is the Year of National Goods, and it seems inappropriate to keep talking about foreign goods. However, we have had the principle of "Chinese learning as the essence, Western learning as the application," so we might as well have a "Cuckoo Day." Fortunately, our country is "founded on agriculture," although the depression of "cheap grain hurts farmers" has not yet disappeared, after all, we cannot even do without the cloth and rice. Grain still needs cloth, and rice still needs to be planted, so it is very appropriate to have a "Cuckoo Day." On this day, rural areas should hold ceremonies and give lectures on basic and practical knowledge related to agricultural affairs, so that farmers can listen and implement improvements, which will definitely be of great benefit. It is much better than pushing foreign goods with "Sacrifice Day," "Cutting Price Day," "Enduring Pain Day," etc., cutting off our own path to survival, and treating shamelessness as interesting.

Avoid 251

— Rong Yu

Do not underestimate this word "avoid". In the history of human life, one cannot do without this page.

"Avoiding debt," "avoiding disaster," "avoiding crime," these are the daily routines of us common people.

"Avoiding birthdays," "avoiding guests," "avoiding the heat," that is not something everyone can do. If you did not knock through seventeen or eighteen wooden fish in your previous life, you will definitely not have this kind of good fortune in this life.

When people are poor, they must borrow money. The faces of creditors are prickly, and when they want you to repay, they will really force you to be helpless. The ancestor of borrowing money was King Zhou Xia. He, with the dignity of an emperor, even built a "debt platform." Did he not meet with creditors? You think the power of creditors is great or not? Nowadays, people have too much debt, so they fly far away and practice debt avoidance. There are also those who owe women money and often hide in bathhouses, which is also a very good method.

Speaking of avoiding disasters, there are quite a few types. The flood comes and confiscates your fields, houses, and livestock into the Crystal Palace. It does not rain for three years, and the land for a thousand miles is barren. You taste the flavor of digging up soil and root. When war breaks out, there are bombs dropped by airplanes overhead; there are big cannon shells and small bullets flying from both sides. When you encounter these three kinds of disasters, are you not going to flee to a safe zone? If you harden your head and say you will not flee, then Yama will definitely take you in.

Young brothers fight over women: poor friends injure people while robbing things. When things happen, they must go out to avoid the limelight. Friends who wield pens, if they are not careful in their words and offend the authorities, it is best to escape as soon as they hear the wind is bad. If the opposition gains power, if you are strong-willed and refuse to surrender, then it is best to take the thirty-six stratagems and flee.

These three kinds of avoidance are bitter, unfortunate, and also something people do not want to accept, but tens of millions of people are trying this taste.

"Avoiding birthdays," "avoiding guests," "avoiding the heat," if you want to avoid all three, you must be a local tycoon. When it comes to your own 45th or 50th birthday celebration; the birthdays of your wife and children; the death anniversaries of your parents, someone will naturally send birthday gifts and pay respects to the birthday star. It is okay to accept all the gifts, but you dare not accept the respects. You avoid it somewhere else to show that you are a humble and honest gentleman. When there are guests visiting on weekdays, if they are higher than me, you might as well welcome them warmly. If they are poor relatives and lame friends, you might as well order the doorman to block them, avoid them, and save a lot of trouble. When the hot summer weather arrives, even if you have installed air conditioning and electric fans at home, you must go to Guling, Qingdao, or Moganshan for a stroll, to show that you are a special class of person.

A lagging gentleman says: Noble people have three avoidances, "avoiding birthdays," "avoiding guests," "avoiding the heat"; poor people also have three avoidances, "avoiding debt," "avoiding disaster," "avoiding criminal punishment." The avoidance of noble people is magnanimous; the avoidance of poor people is often full of sorrow.

Northeast Four Company Commanders 252

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter Ten: Hearing the Words, a Maiden's Heart Alarms; Aspirations for Ennoblement Vanish.

Listening to Songs, Envy Appears; the Body Remains Idle While the Nation Needs Service.

He walked into the room, smiling with a face full of wrinkles, stroking his pale goatee. As soon as he entered, he cupped his hands in greeting towards Guizhi, and said with a smile, "So it's the Yang family's old daughter. We live on the same street, and yet it's been half a year since we last met." Guizhi had no choice but to get up to greet him, giving him a nod. He smiled and said, "How is the old madam? The two of you must be working hard!" Guizhi, upon hearing these polite words from the old gentleman, naturally felt it would be impolite to turn around and leave immediately, so she sat down again. Mr. Niu, having read a few books after all, sat on a broken chair by the window, his face directly facing them. He stroked his beard a couple of times, and then smiled and said, "Why were you mentioning soldiers?" Liu's mother said, "The old girl has moved in next to a company commander. The old master is over sixty years old, and I can't help but worry for him." Mr. Niu nodded and said, "You've been through it yourself; you've become a frightened bird." Liu's mother raised her head and sighed softly, "Don't mention the past. Bringing it up really breaks my heart. My child's father married me, and in fifteen years, we didn't even live together for three full months. For three years in between, he was with the army, and there was no news. If my family hadn't had a bit of money and given me some allowance, I would have starved to death long ago. He always said to me, 'We can't be together often right now, but that doesn't matter, as long as you have enough to eat and drink. Just endure it. Endure it until I become a battalion commander, and everything will be fine.' I believed him, seeing how free many battalion commanders were. It was indeed much better than being a peasant. That's what I thought too. Who told me to marry a soldier? I could only endure it. That year, during the Battle of Nankou, he had already been promoted to company commander, and he was just one step away from becoming a battalion commander. But then, one time, he was ordered to lead a company to seize a mountain pass, and only three men came back. My child's father died in battle that day. I was only thirty-eight years old then, not old, but not young either. What could I do? I could only take my child and endure it.' Speaking of it, that was six or seven years ago now." (115)

Recipes

Various Ways to Enjoy Watermelon 253

— Zheng Yimei

Watermelon is a great way to beat the summer heat. It is prominently displayed in fruit stores and will soon flood the market. According to the "Four Barbarians Supplement," "The Hu people introduced this species during the Five Dynasties period." So, the watermelon we eat today has a Uyghur flavor.

Years ago, I heard that Wu Peifu's wife, Madam Zhang, transported a large batch of watermelons and used the ancient custom of the "watermelon battle" to reward the soldiers. The Master of Xinhange Pavilion wrote a poem about the watermelon battle: "Exciting the three armies to fight, especially marking the watermelon battle with a good name; the general needs to shake Madam's ingenuity; together they compose a poem about the watermelon battle."

Our Jiangsu province produces a lot of watermelons, so Huangdai watermelon seeds are famous throughout the country. Also, the watermelon produced in Fushan, Xikuatang, is praised for its loose, sweet taste and is considered a top-quality product.

People in Weiyang have a small craft, good at making watermelons into lanterns, with delicate figures, landscapes, flowers, birds, and fish. They are lit with candles inside, giving a deep green glow that is quite tasteful. It is a pity that this is a short-lived craft, as the watermelons easily rot.

Eating watermelon with sugar is a common thing. I heard that Americans like to eat watermelon with salt, considering it a delicacy. This is truly a vast difference in taste.

Removing the watermelon pulp and steaming a duck inside is fresh and delicious, called "watermelon duck." Our Jiangsu restaurants often have this dish in the summer.

The watermelons in Bian are very large, almost only one or two per load, each weighing fifty or sixty pounds, which is not surprising. So, several families join together to buy one, otherwise, a small number of people might not be able to finish it.

Seasonal Delicacies 254

— Yi Qiu

I am very interested in cooking. When I was young, I always took over my mother's work on holidays, acting as a cook. The dishes I made were highly praised by my family. Recently, I have also hosted banquets several times due to events and have received unanimous praise from guests. I dare not boast, but although I lack talent in other areas, my talent for seasoning is indeed innate. I will choose a few seasonal delicacies to talk about and reveal my unique methods for the enjoyment of fellow enthusiasts. "Fresh Mushroom Stewed Tofu" "Identification of Mushrooms": Mushrooms are a type of cryptogamic plant. Mushroom filaments are colorless and thread-like, often parasitic on other objects, and have various reproductive methods. Asexually, the tips of the mushroom filaments split and separate, or form umbrella-like or sac-like structures, each containing spores. Sexually, the egg cells of the female organs are fertilized to form zygotes, which gradually germinate and grow, such as pine mushrooms and Huizhou mushrooms. Pine mushrooms and the like, which grow in dry, sunny places, are white or brown in color, have a fragrance, and do not change color when broken and exposed to the air, are non-toxic and edible. Those that grow in wetlands, are brightly colored, and the broken surface turns green, brown, or other colors when exposed to the air, and taste bitter, salty, and pungent, are poisonous and inedible. Vegetable restaurants and mushroom lovers, please pay attention! "Making Mushrooms": Take the non-toxic ones, wash them several times in clear water, and choose the ones with small maggots in the mushroom stems and remove them. Add salt and mix well, and place them in a ventilated place to dry. Then, fry them with sesame oil or soybean oil. You must use several slices of raw ginger in the oil, remove them after five minutes, and you can use them to stew tofu, stir-fry water bamboo shoots, or cook winter melon, all of which taste exceptionally delicious. However, my way of eating is different from others, not frying, not stir-frying, not cooking, but "stewing," called "Fresh Mushroom Stewed Tofu." Take dozens of fried mushrooms, place them at the bottom of a bowl, use tender tofu cubes, cut into small squares, and spread them evenly on top, then cover with seven or eight more mushrooms, add a little salt and sugar, two spoons of soy sauce, and two slices of raw ginger, and stew them in a rice cooker. When the rice is cooked, it is also ready, clear, fresh, and delicious, with a unique flavor. The method is not complicated, and mushroom lovers may wish to try it.

Lotus Leaf Steamed Pork The steamed pork in ordinary restaurants only uses rice flour, and the taste is very ordinary. Even those wrapped in lotus leaves do not pay attention to the freshness of the lotus leaves, and the ingredients and methods are different from what I have prepared. Now that "the lotus leaves reach the sky with endless green," I will describe the method as follows: Use half a catty of top-quality white rice flour, dry-fry it in a pot, fry it until it is yellow but not burnt. Separately, use two ounces of fried black sesame seeds, grind them finely, and mix them into the flour. Buy one or two catties of thin-skinned streaky pork, cut into rectangular pieces (any size), soak them in sesame oil, and pour in two mace of ground fennel, mix and let sit for three or four hours. Take out the pork, pour it into the fried rice flour, coat each piece thinly, and wrap each piece in a fresh lotus leaf. Then, place them in a steamer and steam them for an hour. It will have a different taste, clear fragrance, and be mellow, fatty but not greasy. If you make it according to this method, I can guarantee that you will be satisfied and that it will be far better than the products sold in the market.

However, the number of deliveries outside the exchange by brokers was impossible to verify, estimated at 15 to 16 million. The largest delivery volume was still in the financial sector. A large bank on the Bund delivered about 6 to 7 million, and a large bank on Sichuan Road received 5 to 6 million. In addition, No. 46 delivered 2 to 3 million, No. 50 received more than 2 million, and other scattered settlements were also quite considerable. Deliverers had already obtained good prices, receivers had ample funds, and scalpers also played a significant role. The price process fluctuated greatly. Tracing back to the initial price of 53 yuan on April 29 after the initial military reduction, the initial price was 42.05 yuan on May 1 after the initial tax consolidation, and the initial price was 38.25 yuan on May 15 after the initial consolidation of six. The highest price was 65.85 yuan on June 23 for military reduction, the highest price was 51.5 yuan for salt tax, and the highest price was 53 yuan on June 20 for the consolidation of six. The difference between the highest and lowest prices was 14.1 yuan for military reduction, 11.2 yuan for salt tax, and 14.75 yuan for the consolidation of six, the largest difference. The process took 59 days. Initially, Tianjin was in imminent danger, and Zhangjiakou was under tight siege. Shanxi also reported failure. May 10 to 15 was the most tense period, with the imminent prospect of impending doom. After this, the voices of peace became more and more prevalent. On May 23, the ceasefire agreement had been agreed upon, and the market price rose sharply. On June 5, the US-China cotton and wheat loan failed to materialize, and the majority rose again to the limit, and the market price had a rapid rise and a steady upward trend. As of June 26, the final market price was slightly lower than the previous highest price by 1 yuan for military reduction, slightly lower by 4 corners for salt tax, and slightly lower by 7 corners for the consolidation of six. The overall strength and steady upward trend can be generally seen. The twists and turns were significant, and new high prices were repeatedly discovered. The 96 public price began to see its peak in trading days from mid-June, and the market price also saw its goodness day by day, and did not rise and fall with the rise and fall of other types. The future seems promising. The total transaction volume of various bonds in June was 292.23 million, an increase of 80 million compared to the number in May. Free Talk

On Imitation 275

— Yu Dafu

According to Aristotle of Greece, the origin of art lies in imitation. If the reverse of that reasoning is true, then the Chinese nation is the most artistic nation. Why? Because the Chinese are the most imitative. We dare not say whether it is imitation in a good sense or imitation in a bad sense.

The secret to the Chinese's talent for imitation is, first, imitating the surface without considering the actual substance. For example, everyone knows the benefits of Western culture, and the Chinese must learn from them. So, anyone and everyone puts on Western suits, leather boots, and picks up a cane, thinking that this is all there is to Western culture. Although eating Western food is an exception, it is relatively more practical. Furthermore, when one mentions the preciousness of science, a group of sycophants throughout the country will come out, empty-headed, shouting loudly, "Science, science, science!" But in reality, what is science, how to promote science, how to apply science, all can be ignored. Although in politics, using deceitful tactics to fight for a bit of status and collect hundreds of thousands of "jie jing" (festival respect) and "tan jing" (coal respect) is a more practical, materialistic and scientific method.

The second secret to the easy success of imitation is imitating other people's bad qualities. It's quite obvious. Just listen to the Chinese language spoken by many Chinese children who have received a Western education and those who eat the church's food and the foreign company's tax, and you can immediately see it. They will ignore other things, but only that strange Chinese language spoken by foreigners, everyone can speak it like a foreigner. The frequent inversion of nouns and verbs, the peculiar intonation, if you close your eyes and don't see the yellow, slanted-eyed, snub-nosed face speaking in front of you, you would believe that it is a foreigner teaching you: "Jesus is the very best person!" If the individual is like this, so is the nation. In the past, they yearned for the cold northern countries, but now some people are enamored with a small country in the hot Southern Europe.

The Heart of Youth 276

— Xu Maoyong

In the poem "Autumn Song" (Le chant d'automne) from the collection "Flowers of Evil" (Les fleurs du mal) by the great poet Baudelaire, there are these two lines:

"Like the sun in the Arctic hell, my heart is just a frozen and red ball."

I don't know why Baudelaire had this mood. I am only amazed that these two lines, if used to describe modern Chinese youth, are so appropriate!

People often compare the rising sun to childhood and adolescence, then youth should be the midday sun, and the heart of youth should have boundless light and immeasurable heat. Youths with such hearts should be active, excited, daring to speak, daring to laugh, daring to face reality, and daring to move forward.

However, in China, such youths have not been seen for many years. The hearts of Chinese youths have long lost their light and heat, becoming a frozen and red ball.

There is no shortage of people who blame the youth for their depression and concealment, but they do not look at the Arctic hell that surrounds the youth. Ice mountains, white and terrifying ice mountains, are on the east side, the south side, the west side, and the north side, surrounding them on all sides, with no way out. Even if there are brave men who call on their comrades to open up a path to life, as soon as they speak, they are suffocated by the piercing wind, and as soon as they take a step, they are swallowed up by the snow pit and destroyed one after another.

So, the youth cannot speak, cannot move.

So, the hearts of the youth become frozen and red balls.

However, it is still the heart of youth. So, it can still be red.

Reading "Mother" 277

— Quan Ma

Ding Ling has disappeared, but her "Mother" has been published. Every reader who reads this "posthumous work" (?) will, I think, feel an unnamed sorrow, and at the same time sincerely pray that this female writer will one day return unharmed.

"Mother," it is said, is part of a very grand creative plan, originally intended to write from her mother's era to her own era. "Mother" is written about her mother's era, the Xinhai Revolution era.

However, I believe that the description of the era of "Mother" is not very clear. That is to say, the author's description of the era of the Xinhai Revolution is too vague, too impersonal. This may be due to: (1) the author was not originally from the era of the Xinhai Revolution, and she did not have rich practical life experience of that era; (2) the author's family was originally a "big household." This "big household" is increasingly declining, or the author has heard too much about the decline of this big household from her own mother, so when writing, she will unconsciously harbor a sentimental mood, making more reminiscences of the "Kaiyuan Prosperous Times" (Tang Dynasty) and descriptions of the situation of this declining big household, and cannot actually grasp that era, to draw a clear outline for the movements and changes of that era.

You see, in the 289 pages of the entire book, she spends almost half of the space to describe the declining situation of this "big household" (Jiang family), and in the other half of the space, she constantly recalls the past prosperity of another "big household" (Yu family). She describes the declining situation of the Jiang family and the desolate situation of the orphaned widow very detailed. She also describes the sincere and loyal old family member ("Yao Ma") in great detail. She describes the situation of the Ding family, even the great aunt, second aunt, third aunt, etc. of the Ding family, in great detail. Even Du Shuzhen, who does not occupy an important position in the whole story, is described in great detail. Almost all of these descriptions use the techniques of "Dream of the Red Chamber" to carefully depict, or it can be said to be deliberately imitating "Dream of the Red Chamber." Especially the description of the third young mistress of the Yu family is obviously a replica of Wang Xifeng, and that great nephew's young mistress is obviously a substitute for Granny Liu. In short, she uses "detailed writing" for all these, but for the turmoil and changes of that era, she uses "large writing". It's just a few rough strokes, it's just a faint shadow.

"The world is really different, Yunqing is also different... but his teaching is different from his father's teaching in those days. He doesn't teach people to write articles, but only teaches students how to improve the country, talking about what civil rights are, what a republic is, all are new and strange things."

"What do you understand? Now it's another faction, and the articles have changed."

This is the author's description of this turbulent era, how vague this description is! Also, that is, women (like Mr. Jin and the like) unbound their feet, men (like Yunqing and the like) cut off their long ponytails, that is, the young mistresses and misses sat in sedan chairs and took their old mothers and maids to the newly opened girls' schools. Although it was also mentioned about the Opium War, the Eight-Nation Alliance, and the expulsion of the Manchus, it was only "mentioned", and did not write about the impact that the strong political and economic aggression gave to China, this agricultural country, after the imperialists broke through China's gates, nor did they write about the impact that the Manchurian government's incompetence and tyranny gave to the Chinese masses. Why expel the Manchus? Why reform? Why revolution? These were not explained, so the author's description of the turbulent era before the Xinhai Revolution is obviously "not enough".

Especially the description of the Xinhai Revolution, this great movement, is even more "not enough", even simpler. The explanation of the Xinhai Revolution is only the ghostly panic of the girls' school, only "fearing that the revolutionaries are going to start something, some say in Nanjing, some say in Guangdong, some say in Hankou..." only that night, something really happened, on the side of the examination shed, probably a burst of scattered gunfire came from there... the next day, the streets were quiet and no one dared to open the door. The magistrate had already fled last night. A few soldiers died and some ran away. The rest surrendered. Some ruffians also died. A few old gentlemen who did not shave their heads maintained order in the city, and there were a few young gentlemen with cut hair mixed in, probably the revolutionaries." The author explained the Xinhai Revolution in such an evasive way, as if it was just an accidental storm, not a fully brewed sudden change, as if this "storm" was only unique to Wuling, not a widespread and universal movement. Can such "large writing" give the reader a clear outline of that era? Of course, this attempt has completely failed.

This is just a rough criticism, no, a little thought after reading. There are many other places that seem to have room for discussion, but limited by space, I will have to leave it for later.

The Theory that Nearsightedness is Not a Disease 278

— He Ru

Nearsightedness is becoming increasingly serious recently, and I am quite saddened by my inability to obtain the "Ai Dai" (a type of rare bird) from the Malacca Kingdom. My wife laughed and said: "In this world, nearsightedness is good. Farsightedness is not good." It was a joke, but it had some thought. The Biography of Hermits in the History of the Later Han Dynasty records that Jianwei was appointed to Ren Yong, and Feng Xin of Zitong, both claiming to have glaucoma to avoid the troubles of the world. Yong's wife was adulterous in front, but he concealed the truth and said nothing. Seeing that Yu (the author) had fallen into the well, he endured and did not save him. Xin's maid also had an affair with Xin. When the Shu Rebellion was roughly pacified, they all washed and looked again, saying, "The world is now peaceful, and our eyes are clear." Also, Ruan Ji's Biography in the History of Jin Dynasty says that Ji could show different eyes, giving a "white eye" to those who emphasized rituals and customs. The ancients either soiled themselves with glaucoma or showed contempt with white eyes. Why should I be worried about nearsightedness? The first chapter of "Jin Ping Mei" records that Ximen Qing and Bai LaiGuang, Chang Zhijie, and ten others went to the Jade Emperor Temple to become sworn brothers. Looking around the temple, he caught sight of the Four Marshals, Ma, Zhao, Wen, and Huang. Bai LaiGuang's comments on Marshal Ma's three eyes were also illogical.

Bai LaiGuang held Chang Zhijie's hand and looked over from the left. When he came to Marshal Ma, he saw that the Marshal Ma was majestic and dignified, with three eyes painted above. Then he called Chang Zhijie and said, "Brother, what does this mean? In today's world, it's good to open one eye and close one eye. Is it okay to have an extra eye to see people's flaws!" Ying Bojue heard it and came over and said, "Stupid brother, isn't it good for him to see you with more eyes?" Everyone laughed.

The ancients have said, "It is unlucky to be able to see fish in deep water," let alone see people's flaws! "In today's world, it's good to open one eye and close one eye." This is the subtle meaning of the author of "Jin Ping Mei" in the opening chapter. Although I am nearsighted, I am still better than those who are "眇" (one-eyed) who "open one eye and close one eye." Nearsightedness, nearsightedness, why should it be a disease?

Carrot Top Hair 279

— Written by Jules Renard, Translated by Lin Qu

Carrot Top Hair Photo Album (Continued)

Seven

He could never resist putting both hands in his pockets. As soon as he saw the Lepic family approaching, he hurriedly took them out, but it was already too late. One day, she got angry and sewed his sleeves shut, hands and all.

Eight

"No matter what, you shouldn't lie," his godfather, Mr. Wehrodi, told him. "It's a very bad habit, and what's the use of lying? Everything will always be exposed."

"True," Carrot Top Hair replied, "but we can get through some time."

Nine

The lazy older brother, Felix, barely graduated from school.

He stretched his limbs and sighed comfortably.

"What do you like?" Mrs. Lepic asked him. "You've reached the age to choose a profession. What do you want to do later?" "What! Here it comes again!" said the older brother, Felix.

Ten

Everyone was playing harmless games (jeux innocents).

Miss Palte was being questioned:

"It's because she has blue eyes," said Carrot Top Hair.

Everyone exclaimed:

"That's wonderful! What a charming poet!"

"Ah!" Carrot Top Hair replied, "I didn't even look at her eyes. I said this the same way I say other things. It's a form of habit, a rhetorical figure."

Eleven

When playing snowball fights, Carrot Top Hair stood alone. Because he hid stones in the snowballs, everyone was afraid of him, and his power was great.

He aimed at people's heads and threw: it was quicker that way.

The water was freezing, and while others were skating, he was on the grassy area next door, building another small skating rink.

When playing leapfrog, he was always the one squatting down, letting people leap over his back.

When doing gymnastics, he also let people do whatever they wanted, without regard for his freedom.

When playing hide-and-seek, he hid so well that people forgot about him.

Twelve

The children were measuring their height.

At a glance, the older brother, Felix, who was not in the competition, was a head taller than everyone else. But Carrot Top Hair had to stand side by side with his sister, Elestin, even though she was just a girl. When Elestin tiptoed to make herself taller, Carrot Top Hair, not wanting to displease anyone, secretly lowered himself a little, so that the difference would be slightly larger.

Thirteen

Carrot Top Hair gave the maid Agatha this advice:

"If you want to please Mrs. Lepic, you should say bad things about me in front of her."

But there was a limit to this.

Except for herself, the Lepic family did not allow others to violate Carrot Top Hair.

When a neighboring woman was threatening Carrot Top Hair without permission, the Lepic family rushed over, angrily rescued her son, who already had a face full of gratitude.

"Now, let's settle the score between the two of us!" she said to him instead.

Essays

On Excretion 280

— Wu

Eating big meals, eating pancakes, drinking ginseng soup, drinking tap water, no matter how you eat, no matter how you drink, you have to excrete. This is probably not a problem at all, right? However, the same excretion has different ways of excreting. On this point, I can give many obvious examples.

Speaking of which: Once, I was at the home of a pastor in a small county, and I saw a foreigner shitting. He used a long piece of foreign lead pipe from the bottom of the toilet on the second floor directly to the floor below. Of course, there were many benefits. First, the shitter would not smell his own shit. Second, it could save him from going downstairs. At that time, I thought foreigners were really smart and could come up with such ingenious methods. Later, I realized that the flush toilet in the city was no different from that. However, it was a pity that the small county did not have the large construction of tap water, so a Chinese servant had to carry a bucket of spring water and wait in front of the toilet door. After the foreigner had a big shit, he would pour it down, clean and perfect.

Another time, I heard that there was a young wealthy man named Wang who was very particular about his daily life. When shitting, he had to spread a stack of jade-like Xuan paper on the floor, with his maid serving by his side. Every time he dropped a piece, she would immediately wrap it up and throw it away. This method was of course no less clever than that of the foreigner. Although the shitter was indeed human, and the shit wrapper was also among humans, humanism was no longer as valuable as it used to be. The above two examples are just novelties in small counties and don't amount to much. But once you get to Shanghai, it's very different. Flush toilets can be said to be very common. Anyone who can afford fifty yuan in rent almost has this blessing. As for large hotels, large theaters, and other public places, the excretion facilities are even more magnificent. As soon as you enter the toilet, someone immediately comes forward to serve you. After washing your hands with scented soap, you can adjust your tie and comb your hair in front of the mirror.

However, this is only limited to the special circumstances of the upper class, while the deeply sinful masses of the lower class often suffer for excretion. Many hardworking men, in order to save the two dimes a month for emptying the toilet, and because buying a toilet also costs more than a dollar, have to take advantage of the fact that no one is watching and hide behind the billboards in the open space to relieve themselves. But unfortunately, they encounter the "three-strike patrol". If they don't have time to roll up their pants and escape, they will be taken away after a burst of wooden sticks. The fine is five dollars, or imprisonment for three days. The laws are strict and will not be tolerated. There are also those who usually think that the place where it is forbidden to urinate is the place to urinate, and boldly unleash a torrent from afar. But sometimes fate is unkind, and they will encounter a landlord with a straight face, who will of course scold them and really "send them to the authorities for prosecution without leniency." There are also many country women carrying Longdi Li or chicken eggs who, when there is no other way, have to disregard their womanhood and learn from men to relieve themselves a few times. As for the female workers in the factory, they are a little different. They really want to sneak off to the toilet to take a nap, even though there is a stench that the young ladies can't imagine, but for the sake of rest, they don't need to bring perfume with them.

Because urination and defecation are so inconvenient, excretion has become a source of national wealth. It is said that Hankou once had an official called the "Director of Manure and Urine Bureau", who was fairly appointed through bidding. The income of those who obtained this position was no less than that of the Director of the Opium Prohibition Bureau. However, this was in the past. After the revolution, everything was reformed. Now it is a peaceful and prosperous world, and of course there will be no such smelly business. However, has the government's income not been greatly reduced? This requires a copy of the government gazette.

A Bird's-Eye View of Shanghai's Residential Areas 281

— Kuang

The day before yesterday, a gentleman with the pen name Mr. Wu published a long article in this publication about living quarters, which was quite humorous and profound, prompting me to write this article. But I do not presume to ride on his coattails, and have no delusions of matching his work.

Secondly, because after flipping through a thick Shanghai Guide, I found that the analysis of residential areas was missing and not detailed, which is truly a pity. This makes me want to "supplement it with this", and at least hope that "those who have a Shanghai Guide at home" will consider it for reference.

According to my observation and research, the distribution of residents in Shanghai can be roughly divided into the following areas:

(1) Capitalist District: This area is located in the British Concession, from the Bund westward to Zhao Feng Park on Route Petain. Taking Xizang Road as the boundary, the area to the east can be said to be the capital of capitalists and the place for making money. Large banks, large companies, and large hotels are all concentrated in this area. The number one scenery on the road is grasshopper-like cars and ant-like men in suits. To the west of Xizang Road, such as Jing'an Temple Road, Seymour Road, and Yuyuan Road, is the capital of capitalists, that is, the place where they feel comfortable and enjoy themselves. Western-style houses, villas, gardens, movie theaters, and dance halls are the most outstanding.

(2) Poor People's District: This can be divided into the following two small districts:

(a) Cotton Mill Workers' District: Yangshupu and Xiaoshadu are the main bases. Almost all of Shanghai's cotton mills are concentrated in these two places. Hunchbacked, semi-modern girls and dried-up underage girls swarm like tides in the early morning or evening, and are the only decorations on the road.

(b) Rickshaw Pullers' District: Rickshaw pullers, wheelbarrow pullers, flatbed pullers, and cart pullers mostly live in Zhabei. They shed blood and sweat all day long, but are always hungry, and are directly and indirectly exploited by capitalists. Their bones and blood have created the prosperity of the capitalist district.

(3) Middle Class District: According to my observation, the middle class does not have a fixed area in Shanghai. Perhaps this is because Shanghai has become extremely capitalist. They mostly live in the above two districts, and are interspersed with the poor. In addition, there are several other districts:

(a) Politicians' District: This is in the French Concession. The residences of presidents of parliament, the mansions of ministers, and all kinds of things are here. Fourth- and fifth-class small politicians also rent houses here. If the political situation changes, we can see people who run around like street vendors on some roads in the French Concession. Their political arguments are all for the country and the people, and they are willing to jump into the fire pit themselves.

(b) Remnants of the Old Dynasty District: The pigtails are still reluctant to be cut off, dragged behind their shoulders, or coiled on top of their heads. Such as licentiates and scholars mostly gather in the "quite ancient" Nanshi. Although they are not used to riding in foreign cars, they each have a semi-foreign chartered car. Occasionally, they stroll to bustling areas, such as Nanjing Road, only to shake their heads.

(c) Students' District: This can also be said to be the edge area of Shanghai, from Xujiahui to Fanwangdu, to Jiangwan, to the end of Yangshupu. Several famous universities in Shanghai are in these places. Western-dressed students come and go in the central urban area like carp crossing the river, and are like shuttles weaving cloth. The car business is very good.

(4) Prostitute District: This also refers to the French Concession, such as Dongxinqiao, Xixinqiao, and the vegetable market street behind the Great World, are their activity areas. Late at night, if a fool passes through this area, even if he is spared from being dragged in, he will be frightened and at a loss.

(5) Opium, Gambling, and Loafer District: Also in the French Concession. If you go to the street corner, you can see loafers fighting at any time. Some small hotels can be said to be disguised opium dens. Gambling dens are also everywhere, and gamblers naturally gather in this district.

In conclusion: Shanghai is the general area of Chinese culture and economy, and also the general area of crime and disaster.

Sent to Song, Separated by Walls 282

— Ye

Song,

This letter is the seventh time I've communicated with you. Since you left, your sister has only eaten half a bowl of white rice in two days. She is crying and facing me all day long, wanting me to bring you back. Because your sister cannot live without you, she lives only for you. Today is the third day since you left. She is still not eating or sleeping well, her complexion is sallow and withered. She also lies down during the day and cannot sleep at night. If this continues, the landlord downstairs will easily issue an eviction order.

For the sake of Miss Ye, you resolutely left your beloved sister and me, who is most loyal to you, without saying goodbye. We used to be close and intimate, but once we turned against each other, we became cold and enemies. I have sent you six letters in a few days, but you have not replied. Even though I asked someone to deliver them to you, do you think it's not worth it? In the past, when you came back from school, you often told me things like: Miss So-and-so is so fashionable, so beautiful, Miss So-and-so has many boyfriends, Miss So-and-so likes to watch movies and eat: : :. At that time, I often nodded reluctantly a few times. Afterwards, I slowly persuaded you and told you not to be obsessed with love and go astray. You just smiled and thought that I was praying and couldn't get into your ears. However, although I couldn't force you to listen to me, I honestly taught you like I was teaching you. At that time, I knew you hated me very much, but I didn't keep silent because you hated me. Therefore, I willingly accepted your hatred, hoping that you would repent and change your ways, but the reality was contrary to my hope.

You are now only seventeen years old. If things go wrong, you can still be forgiven. You shouldn't have suddenly left your young sister, because she can't stand on her own.

Moreover, since you met Miss Ye, many of your classmates have criticized you. But apart from the two who hang out with you all day long, who can even be called friends; I have been trying my best to defend you, refute the rumors, and do propaganda. I believe that your knowledge and insights are rich, and that you will not act beyond the scope; therefore, I do not hesitate to expend a lot of effort and become your most loyal defender. But when you came back from school last Sunday, your attitude suddenly changed, and you blamed your beloved sister for no reason. When I spoke to you, you were a little resistant, and then you started cursing. I really don't understand what you mean by doing this; maybe you are deliberately retaliating against me. However, my heart is not made of wood or stone after all, and it only beat wildly for a while at that time.

Afterwards, you practiced a policy of silence towards me. No matter how I tried to persuade you and apologize, you always ignored me. So I lost the trust of your classmates; because your actions unfortunately proved them right. Alas!

Finally, I realized that you had won Miss Ye's favor, and therefore became arrogant. Moreover, you became more and more intimate with those two close friends, as if you had obtained a talisman; because both of them are eager to pursue women!

In the past, you also said that I was jealous and preventing your freedom. In fact, this is just because women are binding you; she can drive your capable heart towards depravity. What is there to be jealous of? Because you think I am obstructing you, you have not returned home once in several days; you are so cruel as to ignore your sister, making her weep all day long as if she had lost something. Ah! You are too cruel.

Song! You must know that this is not ordinary clamor, nor is it intentional insult to you. I hope you will forgive me and realize that what I am saying is right. Get rid of all your temptations and come back to see your beloved and young sister right away! June 27th

On Marriage 283

— Xia Yi

"Let's make it this day!" My father pointed to a line of small characters on the perpetual calendar. This was a standard almanac for determining auspicious days that my father brought from home after a night and a day on the train. This was a book that our government had decided to ban absolutely after deciding to switch to the Gregorian calendar. However, in the Shanghai concession under imperialist rule, people would start shouting and selling "Gregorian-Lunar Calendar Comparison, can't buy it anywhere else!" on the streets every November! The book in my father's hand was just like that.

"Whatever: : :" I couldn't add any other opinion. I have read books for fifteen years, and have also wandered east, west, north, and south for three years. Speaking of age, I am not young. But now, I still have to ask my father for seven or eight hundred yuan a year to spend in Shanghai as a bookworm. I am too embarrassed to suggest any ideas. If I want to be respectable and regard myself as an aspiring, progressive, revolutionary, modern youth, I would say "Let's talk about it in a few years, it's not time to talk about it now." What I mean is, after I become economically independent in a few years. That would be terrible! How many years or decades will it take to become economically independent, enough to build a modern small family? I really don't dare to think about it!

One of my older brothers graduated from university and has been working as an electrical engineer in Shanghai for three years, earning a thousand yuan a year. But after paying for rent, food, clothing, entertainment, etc. every month, his bank savings book always has only five yuan and a few cents in interest, and he never deposits another yuan. He said, "To get married, you have to win the grand prize in the Great Champagne lottery: a woman's pair of silk stockings costs twenty-five yuan." Naturally, women are not easy to deal with, with Paris perfume, high-heeled shoes, and long cheongsams. But how many Chinese women spend twenty-five yuan to buy a pair of silk stockings? How do those writing room clerks who earn twenty yuan a month support a family? If you want to blame someone, you can only blame higher education for ruining people!

As for me, I am considered a spoiled child, and I can't ask for much more. Since it is my father's intention, it is like the school bell has rung. I can only tuck the book under my arm and walk slowly into the classroom. The time of a bookworm is easy to pass. What book is tucked under my arm, and what am I doing in the classroom? Let me tell you slowly!

More News about the "Graduation Examination" 284

— Wu Fei

The Shanghai Municipal Graduation Examination this year, after the unfortunate incident of the test questions being leaked, has caused a lot of criticism from all sides. Some say that there is no need to continue the examination, and some say that the whole thing should be invalid. I believe that cheating is one thing, and the continuation of the examination is another. If the officials who are suspected of cheating are transferred to the court for investigation, then the truth of the matter will come out, and the issue of the continued examination will also be held on the 24th. Although there are still some students who oppose participating, it can be said that it has basically come to an end. Therefore, I will describe what I have heard about the continued examination as follows.

Personally Drafting Questions

During the examination, the test questions for each subject were drafted by outsiders hired by the Examination Committee, with at least two people drafting questions for each subject. Then, the chairman of the committee would gather and select the questions, and then hand them over to a certain printing house in Nanjing to proofread and print. They would be sent to Shanghai one day before the examination to avoid accidents. It cannot be said that the handling was not cautious. However, due to the cheating of officials who did not know how to cherish themselves, there was no good result. Therefore, for the continued examination questions, the chairman of the committee personally drafted them, ordered the staff to print them, closed the room, and opened the lock the next morning. Then, he distributed them to the chief examiners and rushed to each location, which was truly careful.

Perseverance

It was also heard that Mr. Zhang Yuanchun was the proctor for the Nanyang Advanced Business School during the continued examination. Mr. Zhang arrived at the school on time, but there was not a single student. He asked the principal for the school register, investigated the addresses, and then ordered the school servants to drive the Freedom Army at full speed to inform each student individually. It was not until 5:00 p.m. that five students from the junior high school department came to the school. Then, the examination began. His spirit of perseverance to achieve the purpose of the continued examination can be said to be unusual. One of the five students said that he had already found a job, but the qualification for the future must be at least junior high school. He urgently hoped that the continued examination would allow him to obtain a graduation certificate. If so, the ability to handle affairs will be judged based on talent and knowledge, but the qualification issue is indeed somewhat related.

Proportional Extra Points

According to related people, the answer sheets for each subject are being corrected, and the standards are too different. They had no choice but to use the proportional extra points method. For example, if the score is above 30 points, add 25 points. If the score is above 50 points, add 10 points. In this way, everyone can pass. Even those who have already passed will be given some extra points at the discretion of the examiner. It is really impossible to help and all they can do is sigh.

Last Chance

After the continued examination, the list of successful candidates will be published in the near future. However, those who did not participate due to illness will have a make-up examination as originally planned. It is heard that students who did not participate in the continued examination will still be able to participate in the make-up examination. If so, there is still a last chance. Those who still insist on not participating, just because they failed one or two subjects, should consider the issue of further education.

Shop Clerk Communications

Regret Reading Three More Years of Books 286

Dear Editor:

I am a junior high school graduate who wanted to be a shop clerk but didn't get to be one. There are two brothers in our family. My older brother, at the age of fourteen, was recommended by my father to a certain soybean and wheat shop in this port to be an apprentice. At that time, he had just graduated from elementary school. After three years of training, he can actually write and calculate. Now his monthly income is about one hundred and twenty or thirty yuan, which is enough to meet the needs of his small family. As for me! In the year I graduated from elementary school, my father happened to have a slightly larger income, and my older brother was already independent, so he decided to send me to junior high school to continue my studies. Time flies like an arrow, and in the blink of an eye, three years have passed and I have graduated. I want to continue my studies, but my father doesn't have much money, so I have to ask someone to find me a job. I always thought that having read three more years of books, it would be easier to find a job. Little did I know that the opposite was true. Many elders shook their heads and frowned in unison: saying that it is most difficult for junior high school graduates to find a way out. If I go to an old shop to be an apprentice, nine out of ten times I will not be able to endure the hardship and drop out halfway. If I go to a large organization to be a small clerk, my knowledge and experience will not be enough to cope. So until now, it has been two years and ten months, and I still can't find a way in. Alas, whether one can endure hardship or not is different for each person. I believe in myself, I can endure hardship. As for knowledge and experience, of course they are superficial, but how can it be said that junior high school graduates who have read three more years of books are not as good as elementary school graduates! Therefore, every time I hear my father sigh and say "I regret letting him read three more years of books," a strange emotion arises in my heart: Is this really right? Sir, please give me detailed instructions! Please

Yours respectfully, Shen Gantang

× × × ×

Postscript: This matter seems very illogical, but after actual investigation, it is a very common contradiction. The reason why Mr. Shen can't find a job as easily as his older brother is largely due to the fact that the economic situation of society is different from what it used to be. But the fact that junior high school graduates are not welcomed by society is also a fact. The shortcomings of the attitude of the social people towards junior high school graduates have been explained very thoroughly in Mr. Shen's letter. However, the knowledge given to students by three years of junior high school education is mostly outweighed by the arrogance gained in these three years. It cannot be said that there are no exceptions, but it can generally not be denied. Therefore, the elimination of this contradiction requires the joint efforts of three parties. (1) Those in charge of junior high school education should pay attention to this point, so that students can adapt to the environment after graduation. (2) Junior high school students should also give up their arrogance and know that a junior high school graduate is not worth much. They should work with humility, be able to endure hardship, and be willing to learn. (3) Social people should also know that young people are the vitality of the country, and they cannot generalize based on the few unpromising junior high school graduates they have encountered in the past. They should know that people's characters are different, and they might as well give them a chance to try. It is impossible to shirk the responsibility of promoting the younger generation.

Fiction

Under the Red and Green Lights (14) [ 287

— Xi Lin

"Committee Member Chen is out." The messenger threw the contemptuous words like a book at him and closed the door. Although his heart felt as if a heavy burden had been lifted, his face blushed red alone. After hesitating for a moment, he dejectedly walked back the way he came. In the two years of his unemployment, being turned away was commonplace, but the current situation should be somewhat different: during the war with Japan, his own compatriots should be more amicable than usual, right? What need was there to put on airs of importance? Moreover, moreover, he felt hungry again, and touched the only three meal tickets in his pocket. Only Chen Tianren had promised him money to start a magazine: the concept of patriotism began to clash with his stomach: but no matter what, he had to be patient. He consoled and comforted himself with the thought that many important people, before they gained recognition, had to go through this painful stage. After reflecting on this, he prepared to try again this afternoon.

On the way, he bought a copy of the Shen Bao newspaper to read, and he suddenly became happy. Wasn't it true? The news of Zhang Honglie and others organizing the Volunteer Army was published, but Zhou Shaoping's name was missing. Why? Wasn't he the earliest initiator and the most hardworking member? This was ultimately a small matter. As long as the Volunteer Army was indeed established, he would have a share of the credit. He went to find Zhang Honglie, but Zhang Honglie and the others had all gathered at Longhua. It was already eleven o'clock, and his stomach was so hungry that he could no longer bear it. He had no choice but to drag his feet to a restaurant to eat. In the restaurant, he saw several old classmates. At first, they inevitably talked enthusiastically about the war, but when they talked about each other's own affairs, they couldn't help but fall silent.

"How's it going!" One asked with great concern.

"Still the same!" Young people would all answer like this. Even though they had been loyal to each other as classmates, and maybe even had factional disputes, at this moment, a feeling of being scattered and displaced arose, and they couldn't help but feel gloomy and sad.

"I'm planning to start a magazine, and I'd like you all to help me out," Shi Qiao often liked to be self-possessed, always trying to show that he had more tricks up his sleeve than others in his poverty and despair.

"As long as there's money, I'll definitely come!" Wang Hua said bluntly. "But have you found backing yet? And you need to find backing that advocates resisting Japan before they'll put up the money."

Shi Qiao felt that Wang Hua looked down on him too much, but secretly he also admired Wang Hua's sharp eye. But Liu Zhengzhong shook his head and said:

"But how will you write? What effect can it have?"

"Fool! Just speak from the position of the backer, and the effect is: Haha!" Wang Hua was known by everyone as an optimist. His wife lived in a small attic room, eating porridge every day, but he never considered it a shameful thing and never hid it from others.

Shi Qiao didn't completely agree with Wang Hua's words. He believed that running a magazine wasn't that meaningless. If it was run well, and if they spoke fairly, it would certainly be beneficial to the country and society. But everyone knew that Wang Hua was indeed a capable person, and it wasn't appropriate to completely dismiss his words. He couldn't help but invite Wang Hua to his house in the evening to discuss it in detail. After saying goodbye to everyone, he regained his courage and walked towards Chen Tianren's residence.
